We grant that what you mentioned indicates the Qadir, but it is opposed by two types of discourse. The first: to show that the reality of Qadir in the way you said is impossible. Its explanation has several aspects. The first: If the source (agent) has gathered all that is necessary for being a source (negatively or positively), then omission is impossible. If one of the considered conditions is missing, the action is impossible, unless it is said that one thing is a source for the action sometimes and for omission another time without any change in the state in both cases; but that would be a preference of one side of the possible over the other without a preferrer, which is impossible. Also, source-hood on this estimation becomes accidental, because if the flow of the effect from the source depends on a new condition being added to it, what is obtained first is not a complete source; and if it does not depend on it, then the emanation of the effect from that source in a specific time and not another is mere accident. Permitting that entails permitting the transformation of what is possible by itself at one time into necessary by itself at another time, which closes the door to establishing the source. So it is established that capability (al-maskanah) of action and omission is not considered in the reality of Qadir. Confirming that, the school of the Mu'tazila: that violating reward and compensation would necessitate ignorance and need, which are impossible for the Ancient; and whatever necessitates the impossible is impossible; so violating them is impossible, so their emanation from Him is necessary. And the Ahl al-Sunna held that God's will and power are related to bringing into existence specific things, and change in His attributes is impossible, so being an effect-giver is necessary and its opposite is impossible. So the possibility of hesitation is rejected. And from the school of all: that God, exalted, knows from pre-eternity which particulars will exist and which will not; the impossibility of change in knowledge necessitates the impossibility of change in the known; power over the impossible is impossible; so capability in both sides is not considered according to all schools. The second: that capability (al-makanah) in both sides is either established at the time of the occurrence of one of them or before that. The first is false because at the time of the occurrence of one of them, what has occurred is necessary and its opposite is impossible, and the possibility of hesitation between the necessary and the impossible is impossible. The second is likewise, because the condition for occurrence in the future is the occurrence of the future, which is impossible to occur in the present; and what depends on the impossible is impossible. So its occurrence with the condition of being in the future is prevented in the present, and the impossible has no capability. The third: our statement: the Qadir must be hesitant between action and omission; this is only valid if action and omission were both possible. But (here) omission is impossible to be possible, because omission is non-existence, and non-existence is pure. There is no difference between saying 'he was not an effect-giver' and saying 'he effected a non-existential effect'. And because saying 'he did not bring into existence' means that it remained on the original non-existence. So if the current non-existence is identical to what was, ascription to the Qadir is impossible because obtaining what is already obtained is impossible. So it is established that omission is not possible. And if so, it is impossible to say that the Qadir is one who hesitates between action and omission. If you say that omission is the act of the opposite, then the Qadir hesitates between performing a thing and performing its opposite. I say: then it follows that the Qadir is never free from performing one of the two opposites, which leads you to either the eternity of the world or the eternity of its opposite, which you do not hold.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a classification and refutation. Razi explains the first type of opposition: demonstrating that the concept of Qadir (as capable of both action and inaction) is logically impossible. He gives three arguments (وجوه). The first argument: if the agent has all conditions, the effect is necessitated; if a condition is missing, the effect is impossible. To say the agent can act or omit arbitrarily without any change leads to preference without a preferrer, which is absurd. Also, if a new condition is needed, the agent wasn't fully qualified; if not, the timing is arbitrary. This would allow a possible thing to become necessary, which is impossible. Therefore, capability of both is not part of the reality of Qadir. He then notes that even the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunna reject such hesitation in God's case. The second argument: capability (مكنة) can be considered either at the time of the act or before. At the time of the act, the act is necessary; before, the condition (future) is not yet present, so capability in that future sense is impossible. The third argument: if the Qadir must be hesitant, then both action and omission must be possible. But omission is non-existence, which is identical to what was before; thus it cannot be originated by a Qadir because that would be obtaining what is already obtained. If one says omission is the act of the opposite, then the Qadir is forced to always do one opposite, leading to the eternity of the world or its opposite, which is not held.

Key Terms
قادر
ترك
عدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's power includes the ability to not create, i.e., omission is a possible act.
Correction: Razi shows that omission is non-existence and cannot be originated; it is not a distinct act of power.

Checkpoint
According to the third argument, why is omission not a possible object of power?
A) Because omission is evil.
B) Because omission is non-existence, and bringing about non-existence would be obtaining what already exists, which is impossible.
C) Because God always acts.
D) Because omission requires time.

Key Takeaway
Omission cannot be an act of power because it is not a positive entity; it is merely the absence of existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God's ability to act or refrain from acting, have you unconsciously imagined Him as hesitant like a human being? How does Razi's logical dismantling of that analogy challenge your mental image of Allah's power? Will you now strive to purge any trace of human hesitation from your conception of God's will?
?
This argument reveals that non-existence is not a positive thing that God 'does', but simply the absence of His action. In your own life, when you fail to perform an obligatory act, do you treat that failure as a positive 'choice' you made, or as a lack of action? How does this lesson expose the way you might excuse your own sins by framing them as mere omissions? Will you now repent and take responsibility for your neglect?
?
Razi's argument strips away the notion that God's power can be defined by 'hesitation' between opposites. But in your daily supplications, do you ever pray as if Allah might be 'torn' between granting and denying your request? How would your relationship with Allah change if you truly believed that His power is absolutely decisive and free from any passivity? What step can you take today to deepen that conviction?

The Complete Source Must Produce Its Effect
Al-Razi presents the core argument that a complete source must produce its effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a source that possesses all necessary conditions cannot refrain from producing its effect.

Core Idea
A complete source cannot refrain; otherwise, its act would be arbitrary.

Al-Razi begins by challenging the Mu'tazilite notion that a powerful agent must have equal capacity for act and refrain. He argues that if a source possesses everything needed for sourcehood, refraining is impossible. This lesson unpacks that core argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the literal translation. Note the key terms: مصدر, مسكنة, ترجيح بلا مرجح.
The argument moves from conditionals to a reductio ad absurdum.
2
Identify the main conditional argument
Identify the two cases: if the source is complete (possesses all conditions), refraining is impossible; if a condition is missing, the act is impossible.
This is the backbone of the argument.
3
Understand the counterexample and its refutation
Consider the objection that the same source could act or refrain without change. Recognize that this would require a preference without a preferrer, which is impossible.
This shows why the objection fails.
4
Grasp the conclusion about capacity
The argument concludes that capacity for both act and refrain is not essential to a powerful agent. Notice how the reasoning supports this.
This directly rebuts the Mu'tazilite view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول أن المصدر إن استجمع جميع ما لابد في المصدرية سلبا أو إيجابا امتنع الترك ، فإن اختل قيد من القيود المعتبرة امتنع الفعل إلا إذا قيل إن الشيء الواحد يكون مصدرا للفعل تارة والترك أخرى من غير حال البتة في الحالين، لكنه يكون ترجيحا لأحد طرفي الممكن على الآخر من غير مرجح وهو محال وأيضاً فالمصدرية على هذا التقدير تصير اتفاقية ، لأن فيضان الأثر عن المصدر إن توقف على انشياف قيد جديد إليه لم يكن الحاصل أولا مصدرا ،تاما ، وإن لم يتوقف عليه كان صدور الأثر عن ذلك المصدر في زمان بعينه دون آخر مجرد الاتفاق ، وتجويزه يقتضى تجويز انقلاب الممكن لذاته فى وقت ، واجبا لذاته في وقت آخر فينسد باب إثبات المصدر، فثبت أن للمسكنة من الفعل والترك غير معتبرة في حقيقة القادر، وبما يؤكد ذلك أن مذهب المعتزلة أن الإخلال بالثواب والعوض يقتضى الجهل والحاجة المحالين على القديم و مستلزم الممتنع ممتنع، فالإخلال بهما ممتنع فصدورهما عنه واجب . و. ذهب أهل السنة أن إرادة الله تعالى وقدرته متعلقتان بإيجاد أشياء متعينة والتغير على صفاته ممتنع فتكون المؤثرية واجبة ونقيضها ممتنع ، فإمكان المتردد مردود . ومن مذهب الكل أن الله تعالى عالم في الأزل بأن أى الجزئيات توجد وأيها لا توجد وامتناع تغير العلم يستلزم امتناع تغير المعلوم والقدرة على الممتنع ممتعة فالمسكنة في الطرفين غير معتبرة على جميع المقالات .
The first: If the source (al-masdar) possesses all that is necessary for sourcehood, negatively or positively, then refraining is impossible. If a condition among the considered conditions is missing, then the act is impossible, unless it is said that one thing is a source for the act sometimes and for refraining other times without any state at all in both cases, but that would be a preference of one side of the possible over the other without a preferrer, which is impossible. Also, on this supposition, sourcehood becomes accidental, because if the emanation of the effect from the source depends on the addition of a new condition to it, then what first obtained was not a complete source, and if it does not depend on it, then the occurrence of the effect from that source at a specific time rather than another is mere accident, and allowing it necessitates allowing the transformation of the possible in itself at one time into necessary in itself at another time, thus closing the door of proving the source. So it is established that capacity (al-maskanah) for act and refraining is not considered in the reality of the powerful agent (al-qadir). And confirming that is the doctrine of the Mu'tazila that failing to give reward and compensation requires ignorance and need, which are impossible for the Eternal, and that which entails the impossible is impossible, so failing to give them is impossible, so their occurrence from Him is necessary. And the Ahl al-Sunna hold that the will and power of Allah are related to bringing into existence specific things, and change in His attributes is impossible, so causing is necessary and its opposite is impossible, so the possibility of hesitation is rejected. And it is from the doctrine of all that Allah is eternally knowing which particulars exist and which do not, and the impossibility of change in knowledge entails the impossibility of change in the known, and power over the impossible is impossible, so capacity in both sides is not considered according to all statements.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage presents the first argument against the Mu'tazilite notion that a powerful agent must have equal capacity for act and refrain. Al-Razi argues that if a source (like God) has all necessary conditions for producing an effect, it cannot refrain from producing it. If a condition is missing, the act is impossible. The idea that the same source could produce an effect at one time and refrain at another without change is absurd, as it would require arbitrary preference without a preferrer, making sourcehood accidental. The conclusion is that capacity for both act and refrain is not essential to the powerful agent. Support for this is drawn from Mu'tazilite views (reward and compensation must be given, so they are necessary) and from Ahl al-Sunna (God's will and power are fixed, so causing is necessary). Finally, universal agreement that God's eternal knowledge determines what occurs, making change impossible, so capacity for both sides is invalid.

مسكنة
ترجيح بلا مرجح
ممكن
واجب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A powerful agent must have equal capacity to act or refrain.
Correction: Al-Razi argues that if the source is complete, refraining is impossible; thus such equal capacity is not essential.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Razi's first argument, what happens if a source is complete (possesses all necessary conditions)?
A) It can either act or refrain with equal ease.
B) Refraining from the effect is impossible.
C) The act becomes impossible.
D) Sourcehood becomes accidental.

Key Takeaway
If a source is complete, it cannot refrain from producing its effect; otherwise, its act would require an arbitrary preference.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If a complete source cannot refrain from producing its effect, then where in your life are you failing to act because you lack the conditions of a complete source? What conditions are missing, and what are you doing to complete them?
?
The argument shows that arbitrary preference without a reason is impossible. Think of a recent decision you made without clear justification. How does this lesson challenge you to examine your choices?
?
Al-Razi argues that equal capacity to act and refrain is not essential to being a powerful agent. Do you sometimes pride yourself on your ability to do or not do something, thinking it shows power? How does this lesson redirect your understanding of true power?

Support from Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunna
Al-Razi presents doctrinal support from Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunna for the necessity of effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will see how both Mu'tazilite and Sunni doctrines imply that a complete source must produce its effect necessarily.

Core Idea
Both Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunna lead to the necessity of effect for a complete source.

Al-Razi strengthens his argument by showing that even the Mu'tazila, who emphasize God's justice, and the Ahl al-Sunna, who emphasize God's will, both lead to the conclusion that causing is necessary. This lesson explores those doctrinal supports.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two schools
The passage mentions the Mu'tazila first, then Ahl al-Sunna. Read each part separately and note the reasoning.
The word 'وبما يؤكد ذلك' connects this to the previous argument.
2
Analyze the Mu'tazilite argument
The Mu'tazila argue that failing to give reward/compensation implies ignorance and need, which are impossible for God. Therefore, it is necessary for Him to give them.
This shows that even Mu'tazilite premises lead to necessity.
3
Analyze the Sunni argument
Ahl al-Sunna hold that God's will and power are directed to specific things and cannot change, so causing is necessary and its opposite impossible.
This directly supports the necessity of effect.
4
Synthesize the conclusion
Both schools, despite their differences, agree that the effect is necessary from a complete source. This refutes the idea of equal capacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

Eternal Knowledge Necessitates Determinacy
Al-Razi presents the universal argument from God's eternal knowledge to deny equal capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how God's eternal and unchanging knowledge determines all events, making equal capacity for act and refrain impossible.

Core Idea
God's eternal knowledge fixes what will occur, so capacity for both sides is meaningless.

The final argument appeals to a universal consensus: God knows eternally which particulars will exist and which will not. Since knowledge cannot change, the known cannot change, and power over the impossible is impossible. Therefore, the capacity to either act or refrain is not a real attribute of God.

Guided Path
1
Read the short passage
This is a concise syllogism. Read it once, then the translation. Note the term 'المسكنة' (capacity).
The argument is from divine knowledge.
2
Trace the logical chain
God knows eternally which particulars exist. Knowledge is unchanging, so the known (what exists) is also unchanging. Power over the impossible (changing the known) is impossible. Therefore, capacity for both act and refrain is invalid.
This refutes the idea that God could have done otherwise.
3
Understand the conclusion
The conclusion denies 'capacity' (المسكنة) in the sense of equal ability. According to all schools, this capacity is not considered a real attribute of the powerful agent.
This unifies the arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage presents the first argument against the Mu'tazilite notion that a powerful agent must have equal capacity for act and refrain. Al-Razi argues that if a source (like God) has all necessary conditions for producing an effect, it cannot refrain from producing it. If a condition is missing, the act is impossible. The idea that the same source could produce an effect at one time and refrain at another without change is absurd, as it would require arbitrary preference without a preferrer, making sourcehood accidental. The conclusion is that capacity for both act and refrain is not essential to the powerful agent. Support for this is drawn from Mu'tazilite views (reward and compensation must be given, so they are necessary) and from Ahl al-Sunna (God's will and power are fixed, so causing is necessary). Finally, universal agreement that God's eternal knowledge determines what occurs, making change impossible, so capacity for both sides is invalid.

Key Terms
عالم
أزل
جزئيات
تغير العلم
معلوم
قدرة على الممتنع
مسكنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's knowledge does not determine the outcome; He can still act otherwise.
Correction: Since God's knowledge is unchanging and infallible, what He knows must occur; thus, He cannot do otherwise.

Checkpoint
According to the universal argument, why is capacity for both act and refrain not considered a real attribute?
A) Because God's power is limited.
B) Because God's eternal knowledge fixes what occurs, making change impossible.
C) Because the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunna disagree on this point.
D) Because God's will is free.

Key Takeaway
God's eternal and unchanging knowledge determines all events, so the capacity to act or refrain is not a real attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's knowledge of your future actions is absolutely fixed and unchanging, how does that affect the sincerity of your repentance when you know He already knew you would sin? Will you still turn to Him in genuine regret?
?
This passage says God does not have equal capacity to do or not do an action—His will is determined by His knowledge. Does this disturb your intuitive sense of God's omnipotence? If so, what does it reveal about your assumptions of what 'power' means?
?
Al-Razi claims all schools agree on this determinative aspect of divine knowledge. Yet you may feel you choose freely. Where do you actually experience 'capacity' in your own life, and how does that compare to God's lack of equal capacity? What does that contrast teach you about your dependence on Him?

Why Refraining Is Not an Act of Power
Al-Razi argues that refraining (tark) is non-existence, not an act.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Razi's argument that refraining (tark) cannot be an object of power because it is non-existence, and how he defends against the objection that refraining is equivalent to performing the opposite act.

Core Idea
Refraining is non-existence, and non-existence cannot be caused.

Al-Razi here presents a sharp critique of the common definition of the powerful agent as one capable of both act and refrain. He argues that refrain is not a positive action but mere non-existence, and therefore cannot be attributed to a causal agent. This passage also shows how he handles a potential objection that refraining is equivalent to performing the opposite act.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation once to get the overall argument. Note the structure: main claim, reasons, objection, reply.
2
Identify the key reasons
Find the two reasons Al-Razi gives for why refrain is not within power: because it is non-existence, and because it would be 'attaining the attained'.
The phrase 'تحصيل الحاصل' (attaining the attained) is a key technical term.
3
Understand the objection and reply
Notice how the objector tries to define refrain as the act of doing the opposite, and Al-Razi's response that this leads to the agent always being engaged in one of two opposites, implying eternity.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this argument matters for the concept of divine power. How does it challenge the idea that God can choose to refrain from acting?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث قولنا : القادر يجب أن يكون مترددا بين الفعل والترك إنما يصح أن لو كان الفعل والترك مقدورين لسكن الترك محال أن يكون مقدوراً لأن الترك عدم والعدم فى محض ، ولا فرق بين قولنا لم يكن مؤثرا وبين قولنا أثر فيه تأثيرا عدميا ، ولأن قولنا ما أوجد معناه أنه بقى على العدم الأصلي، فإذا كان العدم الحالى عين ما كان استحال استناده إلى القادر لان تحصيل الحاصل محال ، فثبت أن الترك غير مقدور ، وإذا كان كذلك استحال أن يقال القادر هو الذى يكون ترددا بين الفعل والترك ، فإن ذلت الترك هو فعل الضد فالقادر متردد بين فعل الشيء وبين فعل ضده ، قلت فيازمك أن لا يخلو القادر عن فعل أحمد الضدين فيلزمك إما قدم العالم أو قدم ضده وأنت لا تقول به .
The third: Our statement: 'The powerful agent must be hesitant between act and refrain' is only valid if act and refrain were both within power. But refrain is impossible to be within power because refrain is non-existence, and non-existence is pure nothing. There is no difference between our saying 'he did not cause' and our saying 'he had a non-existential effect on it'. And because our saying 'he did not bring into existence' means that it remained in original non-existence. Since the current non-existence is identical to what was, its attribution to the powerful agent is impossible, because 'attaining the attained' is impossible. So it is established that refrain is not within power. If that is so, it is impossible to say that the powerful agent is one who is hesitant between act and refrain. For if you say that refrain is the act of the opposite, then the powerful agent is hesitant between doing something and doing its opposite. I reply: Then it follows that the powerful agent is never free from doing one of the two opposites, and therefore it follows for you either the eternity of the world or the eternity of its opposite, which you do not affirm.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage argues against the definition of the powerful agent as one capable of both act and refrain. Refrain is non-existence, and non-existence is nothing that can be caused; saying 'he did not cause' is equivalent to saying 'it remained non-existent', which is not a causal act. Therefore refrain is not a possible object of power. If one objects that refrain is actually the act of doing the opposite, then the agent is hesitant between two positive acts, which would force the agent to always be doing one of them, leading to undesirable consequences like the eternity of the world. So the original definition fails.

عدم

ضد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That refraining is an action or something that can be caused.
Correction: The passage clarifies that refrain is mere non-existence, not a positive act, and therefore cannot be an object of power.

Checkpoint
Why is refrain not a possible object of power according to the third argument?
A) Because it is an attribute of the agent.
B) Because it is non-existence and non-existence is nothing.
C) Because the agent cannot choose it.
D) Because it requires a separate will.

Key Takeaway
Refraining is not an object of power because it is non-existence, and non-existence cannot be caused.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You often think of your ability to refrain from sin as a sign of your willpower. But if refrain is simply non-existence, then your 'refraining' is not an act you perform—it is just the absence of an act. Does that shake your pride in your self-control? How will you rely on Allah's power to actually do the good, rather than merely avoid evil?
?
If non-existence cannot be caused, then your laziness and procrastination are not positive acts you choose—they are merely the absence of action. Does that make you more or less responsible for them? How will you take concrete steps to bring about existence (good deeds) rather than remain in the comfort of non-action?
?
Al-Razi argues that a powerful agent is not defined by being able to refrain, because refrain is not an act. If God's power is not measured by His ability to refrain from evil (since that would be non-existence), how does that affect your trust in Him when you see evil in the world? Are you tempted to think God 'failed' to act when He allowed evil? What does this lesson teach you about the nature of divine action and restraint?

The First Reason Against Proving Divine Power
Al-Razi presents the first reason against proving divine power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Razi argues that divine power cannot be proven, using the dilemma of eternal vs. originated power and the refutation of the obstacle objection.

Core Idea
Divine power leads to a dead end whether eternal or originated.

Al-Razi's argument here is a sophisticated critique of attributing power to God. He assumes the concept of a powerful agent is intelligible, but then shows that applying it to God leads to contradictions. This passage presents the first reason: a dilemma about the eternity or origination of power, followed by a refutation of a potential objection.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dilemma
First, recognize the two options: divine power is either eternal or not eternal. You'll see why both lead to impossibility.
The dilemma is the core of the argument.
2
Why eternal power fails
Eternal power requires the effect to be possible in eternity, but that's contradictory because the effect has a beginning. Read the reasoning carefully.
Key term: 'soundness of the effect' (sihhat al-athar).
3
Why originated power fails
If power is not eternal, it is originated and needs a cause. That cause leads either to free will (infinite regress) or necessitarianism, both problematic.
This attacks the very concept of a divine free agent.
4
Refutation of the obstacle objection
An objection suggests an obstacle prevents the effect in eternity. Al-Razi refutes it by analyzing the obstacle's nature, leading to a contradiction or absurd consequence.
Understand the two cases: removable vs. permanent obstacle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الثانى : سلمنا أن القادر فى الجملة معقول لكن تعذر إثباته هنا لوجوه . الأول : وهو أنه تعالى لوكان قادرا لكانت قادريته إما أن تكون أزلية أو لا تكون والأول محال ، لان التمكن من التأثير يستدعى صحة الأثر لكن لا صحة في الأزل، لأن الأزل عبارة عن نفى الأولية والحادث ما يكون مسبوقا بالأول ، والجمع بينهما متناقض، والثانى محال لأن قادريته إذا لم تكن أزلية كانت حادثة فافتقرت إلى مؤثر ، فإن كان المؤثر مختارا عاد البحث كما كان ، وإن كان موجبا كان المبدأ الأول موجبا . فإن قلت إنه فى الأزل يمكنه الإيجاد فيها لا يزال، وحاصله أن امتناع الأثر عند قيام المقتضى قد يكون لحضور المانع . قلت المانع ان كان ممكن الزوال لذاته فليفرض إرتفاعه وحينئذ يصح الفعل الأزلي هذا خلف وإن كان ممتنع الزوال لذاته فليفرض وجب أن يكون كذلك أبداً ، إذ لو جاز أن ينقلب ممكنا لجاز أن يقال العالم كان ممتنعاً لذاته ثم انقلب واجباً .
The second type: We grant that the powerful agent (al-qadir) is in general intelligible, but proving it here is impossible for reasons. First: If He were powerful, His being powerful would either be eternal or not eternal. The first is impossible because the ability to cause requires the soundness of the effect, but there is no soundness in eternity, because eternity is the negation of priority, and the originated is that which is preceded by priority, and combining them is contradictory. The second is impossible because if His being powerful is not eternal, it is originated, so it requires an effecter. If the effecter is free, the inquiry returns as before; if it is necessitating, then the first principle is a necessitating cause. If you say: In eternity He is able to bring into existence in what will not cease, and its conclusion is that the impossibility of the effect in the presence of the motive may be due to the presence of an obstacle. I reply: If the obstacle is possible to cease in itself, then let its removal be assumed, and then the eternal act becomes valid—this is a contradiction (khulf). If it is impossible to cease in itself, then let it be assumed it must be so forever, for if it were possible to become possible, then one could say the world was impossible in itself and then became necessary.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage begins a new line of argument assuming the concept of a powerful agent is intelligible but denying its applicability to God. The first reason: if God's power is eternal, then the effect must be possible in eternity, but that is impossible because an effect (created thing) cannot coexist with eternity. If the power is not eternal, it is created and needs a cause, leading to an infinite regress or necessitation. An objection suggesting an obstacle is then refuted: if the obstacle is removable, the effect would have to be eternal; if permanent, the obstacle itself would be eternal, leading to absurd consequences.

Key Terms
قادر
أزلي
حادث
مؤثر
مانع
خلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That eternal power could coexist with a temporal effect.
Correction: The passage shows that eternal power would require the effect to be possible in eternity, which is contradictory because the effect has a beginning, and eternity negates priority.

Checkpoint
According to the first reason, why is eternal power (qadiriyya azaliyya) impossible?
A) Because it would require the effect to be eternal.
B) Because God cannot have power.
C) Because the effect would be possible in eternity, but that is contradictory.
D) Because power is a relation.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's first reason shows that divine power, whether eternal or originated, leads to a logical contradiction or an infinite regress, thus cannot be proven.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just grappled with al-Razi's logical dismantling of rational proofs for divine power. Does this shake your confidence in relying on reason alone to know God? If so, what is the foundation of your certainty? Will you let this impasse drive you to seek knowledge through revelation and spiritual experience rather than philosophical arguments?
?
Al-Razi shows that the obstacle objection leads to absurdity: either an eternal act or an eternally impossible world. Reflect: Are there 'obstacles' in your life that you use to justify postponing obedience to Allah? If the obstacle can be removed, why haven't you removed it? If it cannot, does that mean Allah's command is impossible for you? Will you confront this with sincerity and action?
?
This lesson demonstrates that human reason, when left to itself, ends in contradiction when trying to prove God's attributes. Have you ever felt the limits of your intellect in matters of faith? What does that reveal about the need for divine guidance? Will you humbly accept that some truths are beyond reason and require submission (taslim)?

The Object of Power Must Be Distinct and Pre-Existent
Al-Razi argues that the object of power must be distinct, requiring pre-existence, leading to circularity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Razi's argument that the object of divine power must be distinct from others and therefore must already exist, creating a dilemma.

Core Idea
Power cannot create what is not already distinct and existent.

Al-Razi presents a sophisticated logical argument that seems to undermine the possibility of divine creation. He asserts that for something to be an object of power, it must be distinct and existent before the act of power. This leads to a paradox: if its existence depends on power, it would have to exist before power acts.

Guided Path
1
Read the first part of the passage
Read the Arabic passage from the beginning to the conclusion that a circle (dawr) is impossible. Pay attention to the logical connectors.
Notice how Al-Razi builds the argument step by step.
2
Understand the need for distinction
The passage argues that for power to be related to an object, that object must be distinct from other things. Why is distinction necessary?
Think about how a relation requires two distinct relata.
3
See how distinction implies existence
Al-Razi states that everything distinct is existent (thabit). So the object of power must already exist in itself.
The term 'thabit' can mean established or existent.
4
Grasp the dilemma of circularity
If the object's existence is due to power, then it must exist before power acts (to be distinct) and after power acts, creating a circle (dawr). This is impossible.
This is the core of Al-Razi's challenge to divine omnipotence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : أن المقدور القادر لا بد وأن يتميز عن غيره ، لأن اقتدار القادر عليه نسبة بين القادر وبينه ومالم يتميز المنسوب إليه عن غيره استحال اختصاصه بتلك النسبة دون غيره ، ولا تمكن القادر من الجمع بين الحركة و السواد بدلا عن الجمع بين السواد والبياض يستدعى إمتياز أحدهما عن الآخر ، ولأن كونه قادراً على إيجاد الحركة بدلا عن السكون ، وبالعكس يستدعى إمتياز كل واحد منهما عن الآخر ، فإن التردد بين الشيئ بن يتوقف على مغايرتهما ، فثبت أنه لا بد من التميز وكل متميز ثابت ، فإذا تعلق القدرة به يتوقف على ثبوته في نفسه ، فلو كان ثبوته لأجل القدرة لزم الدور ولزم إثبات الثابت وأنه محال. . فإن قلت شرط التعلق تحقيق الماهية والحاصل على التعلق هو الوجود . قلت فالذات لما كانت متقررة قبل التعلق لم تكن مقدورة ، لأن إثبات الثابت محال فالمتعلق هو الذي ليس بثابت وهو إما لو جود أو موصوفية الذات بالوجود الكن ذلك محل ، لأنا بينا أن المتعلق متميز والمتميز ثابت ، فإذا ليس بثابت فهو ثابت هذا خلف .
The second: The object of power (al-maqdur) of the powerful agent must be distinct from other things, because the powerful agent's being powerful over it is a relation between the powerful and it, and without the object being distinguished from others, its specification with that relation over others is impossible. And the possibility of the powerful agent combining motion and blackness instead of combining blackness and whiteness requires distinction of one from the other. And because his being powerful over bringing about motion instead of rest, and vice versa, requires distinction of each one from the other, for hesitation between two things depends on their difference. So it is established that distinction is necessary, and everything distinct is existent. If power is related to it, it depends on its existence in itself. So if its existence were due to power, a circle would follow, and the establishment of what is already established would follow, which is impossible. If you say: The condition of relation is the realization of the quiddity, and what results from relation is existence. I reply: Since the essence was determined before the relation, it was not an object of power, because establishing the established is impossible. So the related is that which is not established, and that is either existence or the attribution of the essence by existence—but that is a matter of discussion. For we have shown that the related is distinct, and the distinct is existent. So if it is not established, it is existent—this is a contradiction.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage argues that the object of power must be distinct from others, which implies it already exists. That creates a dilemma: either its existence is independent of power, so power does not cause it, or power causes it, leading to circularity (it must exist before power acts). An objection that power merely realizes a quiddity is refuted: if the essence is already determinate, it exists, so power cannot produce it; if not, then it is not distinct, contradiction. Thus divine power over creation is problematic.

Key Terms
مقدور
قادر
تميز
ثابت
دور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Power can create something from nothing without any pre-existing distinct object.
Correction: Al-Razi shows that for power to be directed at something, that thing must already be distinct and existent, leading to circularity if power causes its existence.

Checkpoint
What problem arises if the existence of the object of power depends on the power itself?
A) The object would be eternal.
B) A circle (dawr) would result.
C) The power would be temporal.
D) The object would be impossible.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's argument poses a challenge to the notion of divine power creating from nothing by showing that the object must pre-exist.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This argument shows that for power to be directed at something, that thing must already be distinct and existent in your mind. Is there an area of your life where you are trying to 'create' a new habit or virtue without first acknowledging its distinct reality? What would it look like to first 'distinguish' what you are striving for before taking action?
?
Al-Razi notes that hesitation between two opposites requires each to be distinct. When you are torn between two choices (e.g., truth vs. comfort, obedience vs. desire), have you truly distinguished the nature of each option? How does recognizing their distinctness impact your decision?
?
The argument exposes an impossible circle: if the object's existence depended on the power that relates to it, it would need to exist to be related. Reflect on a dependency in your life—perhaps a reliance on a relationship or a possession. Are you caught in a circle where you need that thing to be who you are, yet you are also trying to define yourself without it? How can you break the circle?

The Objection and Refutation: Power and the Realization of Quiddity
Al-Razi refutes the objection that power relates to quiddity, showing it still requires pre-existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection to Al-Razi's circularity argument and his refutation that the object must either be already existent or contradictory.

Core Idea
Power cannot merely realize a quiddity; the quiddity must already be distinct.

Al-Razi anticipates an objection: perhaps power does not bring existence but rather realizes a quiddity. He counters by showing that the quiddity must already be determinate and hence existent, or else it is not distinct. This reinforces his original point.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and reply
Read the second part of the passage starting from 'fa-in qulta' (if you say) to the end. Identify the objection and Al-Razi's response.
The objection tries to separate quiddity from existence.
2
Understand the objection
The objector says that the condition for power's relation is the realization of the quiddity, not existence. Existence results from the relation, not power itself.
This would avoid the circle because quiddity pre-exists in a sense.
3
See Al-Razi's refutation
Al-Razi replies that if the essence (dhat) is already determined before the relation, then it already exists, so power cannot cause it; if it is not determined, then it is not distinct, contradicting the earlier proof.
He uses the same premise that the related must be distinct.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : أن المقدور القادر لا بد وأن يتميز عن غيره ، لأن اقتدار القادر عليه نسبة بين القادر وبينه ومالم يتميز المنسوب إليه عن غيره استحال اختصاصه بتلك النسبة دون غيره ، ولا تمكن القادر من الجمع بين الحركة و السواد بدلا عن الجمع بين السواد والبياض يستدعى إمتياز أحدهما عن الآخر ، ولأن كونه قادراً على إيجاد الحركة بدلا عن السكون ، وبالعكس يستدعى إمتياز كل واحد منهما عن الآخر ، فإن التردد بين الشيئ بن يتوقف على مغايرتهما ، فثبت أنه لا بد من التميز وكل متميز ثابت ، فإذا تعلق القدرة به يتوقف على ثبوته في نفسه ، فلو كان ثبوته لأجل القدرة لزم الدور ولزم إثبات الثابت وأنه محال. . فإن قلت شرط التعلق تحقيق الماهية والحاصل على التعلق هو الوجود . قلت فالذات لما كانت متقررة قبل التعلق لم تكن مقدورة ، لأن إثبات الثابت محال فالمتعلق هو الذي ليس بثابت وهو إما لو جود أو موصوفية الذات بالوجود الكن ذلك محل ، لأنا بينا أن المتعلق متميز والمتميز ثابت ، فإذا ليس بثابت فهو ثابت هذا خلف .
The second: The object of power (al-maqdur) of the powerful agent must be distinct from other things, because the powerful agent's being powerful over it is a relation between the powerful and it, and without the object being distinguished from others, its specification with that relation over others is impossible. And the possibility of the powerful agent combining motion and blackness instead of combining blackness and whiteness requires distinction of one from the other. And because his being powerful over bringing about motion instead of rest, and vice versa, requires distinction of each one from the other, for hesitation between two things depends on their difference. So it is established that distinction is necessary, and everything distinct is existent. If power is related to it, it depends on its existence in itself. So if its existence were due to power, a circle would follow, and the establishment of what is already established would follow, which is impossible. If you say: The condition of relation is the realization of the quiddity, and what results from relation is existence. I reply: Since the essence was determined before the relation, it was not an object of power, because establishing the established is impossible. So the related is that which is not established, and that is either existence or the attribution of the essence by existence—but that is a matter of discussion. For we have shown that the related is distinct, and the distinct is existent. So if it is not established, it is existent—this is a contradiction.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage argues that the object of power must be distinct from others, which implies it already exists. That creates a dilemma: either its existence is independent of power, so power does not cause it, or power causes it, leading to circularity (it must exist before power acts). An objection that power merely realizes a quiddity is refuted: if the essence is already determinate, it exists, so power cannot produce it; if not, then it is not distinct, contradiction. Thus divine power over creation is problematic.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Razi argues that establishing the established is impossible—you cannot cause what already exists. In your own life, where have you been trying to 'create' something that Allah has already decided or decreed? How does this lesson expose the futility of resisting divine will?
?
If the object of power must already be distinct and existent, then what does that say about your own attempts to 'make things happen' without acknowledging the pre-existing reality set by Allah? How will you surrender more fully to His determination?
?
The contradiction in the objection arises from assuming that power can relate to a non-distinct quiddity. Reflect: Do you ever assume that you can change fundamental aspects of your existence—your nature, your past, your limitations—by sheer will? How does this lesson call you to accept what is already 'thabit' and focus on what is truly within your power?

Third Reason: Impossibility of Re-Powering an Existing Object
Al-Razi argues the impossibility of re-exercising power on an existing object.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's argument that after an object is created, it can no longer be an object of power because bringing the existent into existence is impossible.

Core Idea
Once created, an object cannot be re-powered because its existence is already actual.

Al-Razi presents the third reason against the Ash'ari view of continuous power. He argues that if God's power is eternal and He creates an object, that object ceases to be an object of power once it exists. This challenges the idea that power remains attached to the same object after creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the third reason passage
Read the Arabic and translation for the third reason. Notice the logical structure: conditional premise, then contradiction.
The passage is only a few lines.
2
Identify the key logical move
Al-Razi says 'if He were powerful from beginning to eternity, then when He brings it into existence, it does not remain an object of power'. Why? Because bringing the existent into existence is impossible.
3
Understand the relational term
The term 'ta'alluq' (relation) appears as 'tafalluq' in OCR. It refers to the relationship between power and its object. After creation, that relation perishes.
The text says 'that old relation has perished' — meaning the relation of power to the object before creation.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The conclusion is that the effecter (God) does not act except by necessitation, but here the focus is on the impossibility of re-powering an existing object.
This argument is part of a larger proof that power creates its object only at the moment of creation, not continuously.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : لو كان قادراً من الأول إلى الأبد ثم إذا أوجده لم يبق مقدور الاستحالة إيجاد الموجود وذلك التفلق القديم قد فنى وعدم النديم محال . الرابع : إذا قلنا القادر يمكنه أن يوجد فالموجدية ليست عبارة عن نفس الأثر ، أما أولا فلان الموجودية صفة الموجود والأثر قد لا يكون صفة له ، فإن العالم ليست صفة الله تعالى ، وأما ثانيا فلانا إذا قلنا الأثر إنما وجد بالقادر لأن القادر أوجده فلو كان المفهوم من قولنا أوجده نفس وجود الأثر ، لكنا قد قلنا إنما وجد الأثر الأنه وجد الأثر فيكون الحاصل أنه وجد الأثر بنفسه ، وذلك محال ، فظهر أن الموجودية صفة للموجد فهي إن كانت مسكنة الوجود واقعة بالقادر المختار عاد التقسيم فيه وإن كانت واجبة وجب وجود الأثر لأن الموجدية بدون وجود الأثر البتة محال عقلا ، فثبت أن المؤثر لا يفعل إلا على سبيل الإيصاد .
The third: If He were powerful from the beginning to eternity, then when He brings it into existence, it does not remain an object of power because bringing the existent into existence is impossible, and that old relation has perished, and the non-existence of the perpetuity is impossible. The fourth: If we say the powerful agent can bring into existence, then 'bringing into existence' (al-mujidiyya) is not the same as the effect itself. First, because 'being brought into existence' is a property of the existent, and the effect may not be a property of Him—for the world is not a property of Allah. Second, because if we say the effect exists only by the powerful agent because the powerful agent brought it into existence, if the meaning of 'brought it into existence' were just the existence of the effect, then we would have said 'the effect exists because it exists', so the result is that the effect exists by itself, which is impossible. So it appears that 'being brought into existence' is a property of the bringer. So if it is a possible state of existence occurring by the free powerful agent, the division applies to it; if it is necessary, then the existence of the effect is necessary, because the bringer without any existence of the effect is rationally impossible. So it is established that the effecter (al-mu'aththir) does not act except by way of necessitation (al-iysad).
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage combines two short reasons. The third: after an object is created, it cannot be an object of power again (since it already exists), and the original relation of power perishes, leading to impossibility. The fourth argues that 'bringing into existence' is a property of the cause, not the effect. If it were identical to the effect's existence, we would have tautology. Thus 'bringing into existence' is either possible (implying choice) or necessary; if necessary, the effect must exist, so the cause necessitates. Hence the effecter only acts by necessitation.

Key Terms
مقدور
موجود
إيجاد
تعلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's power remains attached to a created object after it exists.
Correction: Al-Razi shows that once an object exists, it cannot be an object of power because bringing the existent into existence is impossible.

Checkpoint
What is al-Razi's main point in the third reason?
A) God's power is not eternal.
B) Once an object exists, it cannot be an object of power again.
C) Power and object are identical.
D) The relation perishes but can be renewed.

Key Takeaway
The existence of an object precludes it from being re-created or re-powered, so divine power's relation to its object is only at origination.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever imagine God’s power as limited like human power, assuming He needs to 're-do' things or sustain by repeating acts? How does this lesson correct that assumption?
?
If God’s power only relates to creation at the moment of origin, what does that mean for your dependence on Him now? How does it reshape your understanding of reliance on God’s continuous care?
?
Al-Razi argues that bringing the existent into existence is impossible. How does this truth affect your awe of God’s creative act? Do you fully appreciate that your very existence is a unique, unrepeatable act of divine power?

Fourth Reason: Bringing into Existence as a Property of the Cause
Al-Razi argues that 'bringing into existence' is a property of the cause, leading to necessitation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's argument that 'bringing into existence' is a property of the cause, not the effect, and that it leads to necessitation.

Core Idea
If 'bringing into existence' were the effect's existence, the effect would cause itself — an absurdity.

Al-Razi's fourth reason is longer and more subtle. He argues that the term 'bringing into existence' (mujidiyya) refers to a property of the agent, not the effect. If it were identical to the effect's existence, we would have a circular explanation. The argument leads to the conclusion that the effecter acts only by necessitation (iysad), which is a key point in al-Razi's theological determinism.

Guided Path
1
Read the fourth reason passage
Read the Arabic and translation for the fourth reason. Notice the two sub-arguments: first about property, second about tautology.
2
Understand 'mujidiyya'
Al-Razi starts by clarifying that 'bringing into existence' is not the same as the effect. It is a property of the cause.
First point: 'being brought into existence' is a property of the existent, and the effect may not be a property of Allah.
3
Follow the tautology argument
If 'brought it into existence' meant just the existence of the effect, then we'd say 'the effect exists because it exists', which is circular and absurd.
4
Consider the two possibilities
Al-Razi then considers two options for 'mujidiyya': either possible (implying free choice) or necessary. If necessary, the effect must exist, so the cause necessitates.
The text says: 'if it is a possible state... the division applies; if it is necessary, then the existence of the effect is necessary'.
5
Grasp the conclusion
The final claim: 'the effecter does not act except by way of necessitation'. This is a deterministic conclusion.
This is a key theological position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : لو كان قادراً من الأول إلى الأبد ثم إذا أوجده لم يبق مقدور الاستحالة إيجاد الموجود وذلك التفلق القديم قد فنى وعدم النديم محال . الرابع : إذا قلنا القادر يمكنه أن يوجد فالموجدية ليست عبارة عن نفس الأثر ، أما أولا فلان الموجودية صفة الموجود والأثر قد لا يكون صفة له ، فإن العالم ليست صفة الله تعالى ، وأما ثانيا فلانا إذا قلنا الأثر إنما وجد بالقادر لأن القادر أوجده فلو كان المفهوم من قولنا أوجده نفس وجود الأثر ، لكنا قد قلنا إنما وجد الأثر الأنه وجد الأثر فيكون الحاصل أنه وجد الأثر بنفسه ، وذلك محال ، فظهر أن الموجودية صفة للموجد فهي إن كانت مسكنة الوجود واقعة بالقادر المختار عاد التقسيم فيه وإن كانت واجبة وجب وجود الأثر لأن الموجدية بدون وجود الأثر البتة محال عقلا ، فثبت أن المؤثر لا يفعل إلا على سبيل الإيصاد .
The third: If He were powerful from the beginning to eternity, then when He brings it into existence, it does not remain an object of power because bringing the existent into existence is impossible, and that old relation has perished, and the non-existence of the perpetuity is impossible. The fourth: If we say the powerful agent can bring into existence, then 'bringing into existence' (al-mujidiyya) is not the same as the effect itself. First, because 'being brought into existence' is a property of the existent, and the effect may not be a property of Him—for the world is not a property of Allah. Second, because if we say the effect exists only by the powerful agent because the powerful agent brought it into existence, if the meaning of 'brought it into existence' were just the existence of the effect, then we would have said 'the effect exists because it exists', so the result is that the effect exists by itself, which is impossible. So it appears that 'being brought into existence' is a property of the bringer. So if it is a possible state of existence occurring by the free powerful agent, the division applies to it; if it is necessary, then the existence of the effect is necessary, because the bringer without any existence of the effect is rationally impossible. So it is established that the effecter (al-mu'aththir) does not act except by way of necessitation (al-iysad).
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage combines two short reasons. The third: after an object is created, it cannot be an object of power again (since it already exists), and the original relation of power perishes, leading to impossibility. The fourth argues that 'bringing into existence' is a property of the cause, not the effect. If it were identical to the effect's existence, we would have tautology. Thus 'bringing into existence' is either possible (implying choice) or necessary; if necessary, the effect must exist, so the cause necessitates. Hence the effecter only acts by necessitation.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'bringing into existence' is simply the effect's existence.
Correction: Al-Razi shows it is a property of the cause, not the effect, and leads to necessitation.

Checkpoint
What does al-Razi conclude from the fourth reason?
A) The effecter acts freely.
B) The effecter acts only by necessitation.
C) Power is not eternal.
D) The effect does not exist.

Key Takeaway
The property of 'bringing into existence' is in the cause, not the effect, and implies necessitation, not free choice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's act of bringing you into existence was a necessary consequence of His essence, not a free choice, does that make you feel like a mere puppet? How does that affect your sense of gratitude and responsibility before Him?
?
You claim to believe that everything happens by God's will, but do you actually live as if your daily choices are also necessitated by Him? Or do you secretly assume your own independent power? Examine one area of your life where you act as if you are the ultimate cause.
?
The argument concludes that the effecter 'does not act except by way of necessitation.' If that is true, then your faith, your worship, your very existence are all directly necessitated by Allah. Does that thought fill you with awe and submission, or with unease? Be honest: which reaction dominates, and why?

Defending Free Agency: Replies to Two Objections
Al-Razi answers two objections regarding the source's occasional effect and capacity for future objects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Razi's replies to two objections concerning the source's occasional effect and capacity for future objects, and how these replies uphold the doctrine of free agency.

Core Idea
A free agent can choose to act or not without external preference.

Al-Razi responds to two objections against his occasionalist position. The first objection questions why a complete cause sometimes fails to produce its effect; the second concerns the capacity for future objects. His concise answers reaffirm the role of free choice and clarify the temporal scope of ability.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage slowly. Then read the literal translation. Notice the brief style and the mention of two objections.
The text has OCR issues; 'المندور' likely means 'المقدور' (the object of power).
2
Identify the two objections and their answers
The passage presents two objections (المعارضة الأولى والثانية) followed by their answers. Identify what each objection claims and how Al-Razi responds.
The first objection is about the source sometimes not acting; the second about capacity for future things.
3
Connect the answers to free agency
Reflect on how Al-Razi's answers defend his view of free agency. The first answer invokes the concept of tarjih bila murajjih. The second answer clarifies that capacity is relative to the object before its existence, not in the present over a future thing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنا المعارضة الأولى: الجوابها أنه لم لا يجوز أن يكون المؤثر المستجمع مجميع جهات المؤثرية تارة يكون مصدراً الأثر وتارة لا يكون ، ونحن قد بينا أن المختار هو الذي يمكنه الترجيح لا لمرجح . وأما الثانية الجوابها : إما التمكن ثابت بالنسبة إلى المندور قبل دخوله في الموجود حوله لامكنة في الحال علي الشيء الذي سيوجد في الاستقبال
As for the first objection: Its answer is that why is it not permissible that the effecter that possesses all aspects of effecthood sometimes be a source of the effect and sometimes not? And we have shown that the free agent is the one who can prefer without a preferrer. As for the second objection: Its answer is that ability (al-tamakkun) is established with respect to the object of power before its entry into existence around it? There is no ability in the present over the thing that will exist in the future.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage provides brief replies to two objections. The first objection seems to claim that a complete source can sometimes act and sometimes not; al-Razi answers by reiterating that the free agent can prefer without a preferrer, which is the core of voluntarism. The second objection concerns capacity for future objects; al-Razi states that ability is relative to the object before its existence, but there is no present capacity over a future thing. The text is somewhat unclear at the end.

Key Terms
مؤثر
مختار
ترجيح بلا مرجح
تمكن
مقدور
استقبال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A complete cause (al-mu'aththir) necessarily always produces its effect.
Correction: Al-Razi holds that a free agent can choose to act or refrain without any external preference, so the effecter may sometimes not produce the effect.

Checkpoint
According to the answer to the first objection, what characterizes the free agent (al-mukhtar)?
A) He cannot refrain from acting.
B) He can prefer without a preferrer.
C) He is necessitated.
D) He has eternal power.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi defends free agency by asserting that a complete source can refrain from acting, and that capacity for future objects is established only before their existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you plan for the future, do you truly believe that God's power encompasses every event before it happens? How does that change the way you rely on your own plans? This week, consciously remind yourself when making a plan that your ability is only established before the action, not in the present moment over the future. Write down one decision you will entrust entirely to God.
?
Al-Razi says a free agent can choose without external cause. When you sin, do you blame circumstances or others for your choice? Reflect on a recent wrong decision. Confess that you had no external compulsion, only your own free will. Make a commitment to take full responsibility for one choice today.
?
Consider something you hope to achieve in the future. According to this lesson, capacity is established before the action exists, not in the present over the future. How does that affect your current sense of ability or inability? What step can you take now to act in faith, trusting that your capacity is already granted by Allah?
